<response>None</response>< Text>
Come play Magic The Gathering here. I guess they have other games but you should sell those other cards back to the store and just play Magic. If you're playing Yu-Gi-Oh you're not living your life right and your mother wants you to move out of her garage, if you play Dragon Ball Z it's because Super Saiyan Goku is your hero and if he went to your JR High he definitely would be your friend. The Blackstone Owl also has a great selection of board games,  D&D materials, and if you're a Magic player with a girlfriend and not a lonely DBZ player, they sell Loungefly Purses and other assorted accessories so you can grab your girl a present while you play Magic the day before your anniversary. If you aren't coming here for all of your collectible card game needs then you should be, get your life together and stop buying those Pokemon blister packs at Target and just get what you need at the Blackstone Owl.< /Text>

< review>
Roxy's Boutique provided such bad customer service that I would not get married again if given the choice.

On my first visit, the staff was super friendly. I felt welcomed and was happy to have come upon a store with such friendly staff. Boy was I wrong. Friendly Freddy, or so I thought so, sold me up on a dress (which would include the veil and the tailoring) and scheduled my next appointment. A deposit needs to be given just for them to bring the dress.

I called multiple of times to confirm my second appointment which was at 10:30am. No answer. I started to freak out. I arrived on time to find another lady also waiting for the store to open. She informed me that the store had been canceling on her the whole week due to excuses such as "accidents", "the dress not being ready," and so on. I felt horrible for this lady as she was getting married the next day and still hadn't received her dress. The lady and I remembered that staff at Roxy's Boutique had told us they were the same at CINDERELLA'S CLOSET. We walked together and found Freddy providing service to another customer. By now it was 11am! I told Freddy I had my appointment at 10:30am and he was the one who scheduled it. He now claimed that he had nothing to do with the other store, even though he wrote his name on the contract he had given me. The lady and I went back to Roxy's Boutique. It finally opened past 11am. We were greeted by Leslie who told the lady her dress wouldn't be in until 2pm. The lady was furious at the fact that she had been calling the whole week and they never gave her a specific time. The lady for the meanwhile left, and I informed Leslie that my appointment was at 10:30am and she lashed out at me. She claimed and showed me that I was scheduled for 11am in their binder. I tried showing her my contract with the time of 10:30am, but she responded by YELLING, "Us staff have the same rights as you customers!" At this point I wanted to get my deposit back and take my business elsewhere, but I knew that wasn't an option. Leslie fitted my dress and scheduled my next appointment. They ask for the full amount of the cost of the dress before they start tailoring it.

I asked for the day off from work for my next appointment. I called multiple times before and on my way to my next appointment. When they finally answered and told me the dress wasn't ready, I was already nearby (I live 2 hours away). They rescheduled me.

I asked for the day off from work for my rescheduled appointment. When I arrived, the store looked different. I was greeted by Julio/Julian. He informed me that the store now had a new owner (after further conversation with staff, I learned the new owner is still within family/family friends). However, they had my dress. I wasn't able to try it on during my scheduled time because we had to wait for another lady to come. She was a young lady about the age of 17. When I tried on the dress, it was still too long. A tailor was brought in and told me she could fix the dress, but I would have to come back. I was no longer willing to go back due to losing days of work and the commute; This was supposed to be my last visit. I tried getting compensation back for at least the tailoring part of the dress since I would have to pay someone else to fix it, but I was told no refunds were given, even though they didn't do the job correctly. There is a quote that says, "Arguing with an idiot makes two of them," and by this point I was over the whole experience that I just wanted to leave and never come back. ¬†I took my dress and was able to find a tailor as soon as I arrived home. The new tailor showed me how the dress was fixed by Roxy's Boutique, and all the tailoring was horrible!

Horrible experience and customer service. After being sold on a dress by friendly staff, appointments were never on time, cancelations were last minute, tailoring was not correct, and no refunds were given for not completing their job correctly on tailoring the dress. Spare yourself the trouble, panic and anxiety attacks of giving your business to Roxy's Boutique.< /review>

I was so impressed with the selection of pianos and the proprietor Russell Kassman, that I bought my piano there! <review>My wife and I met because of our love of pianos. She is a classically trained pianist, and I am a piano instructor that her sister hired for her daughter. Long story short, collecting pianos and other instruments is one of our many interests. We truly enjoy an opportunity to visit a piano gallery, and when we moved to California from the east coast, we went searching for the best piano dealers. We have some extra space in our new home, and were playing the idea of adding to our collection.

We visited R. Kassman Pianos a few weeks ago, and we were very impressed. We have high expectations, and while some of the first places we checked out on the West Coast didn't impress us much, the selection at R. Kassman is beautiful and unique. Nothing typical. I love an instrument with a good story, and there is no shortage of good stories.

Some other piano galleries have lovely pianos, but don't have the expertise to properly repair some of them. It has ruined more than a few pianos I have encountered that just were not up to par anymore because they were improperly maintained. The pianos that we looked at here had been carefully researched and kept in their original state as much as possible.

I saw a few pieces similar to those I had looked at on the East Coast, and when I checked prices, I found that they were priced well. R. Kassman isn't an individual that is out to make a quick dollar from his customers, and I found my knowledge and interest were welcomed here... The staff are just as sharp</review>< Pics>

<text>I bought a piano at Kassman this afternoon, and for me, it was an excellent experience. There's a widely varying opinion about this shop in these comments, and I think there's a good deal of confusion too. Here's how I see it.

Although Kassman looks like a run-of-the-mill piano shop from the outisde, that's not what it is. Don't expect to walk in, take a look around, turn yourself or your kids loose to plink a few keys, and think that since you're the customer, you're always right. You're not. Russell, the gentleman who owns the shop, clearly posts that his shop serves customers by appointment only, and if you can't follow this simple rule, don't be shocked if he turns you away. It might be better if you don't think of this shop as a retail store at all. Really, it's nothing like Walmart or Target, nor is it like most other piano shops.

Russell is a specialist, and if you think of him like he's a Doctor of Pianos (a Pianologist?), you'll do better from the start. Just imagine if you were to walk into a dermotologist's office unannounced, barge into an examination room where the doctor is already seeing someone, declare that you've got an itch you want looked at right away, and that you'll just fidget with the equipment in the office while you wait for the doctor to finish up with the other patient. You'll almost certainly be asked to leave and not come back. What's more, no sensible person would blame the doctor in this situation, or complain that the office gives bad service.

The key to having a good experience at Kassman is to know what you're getting into. You need to be serious about buying a piano. You need to have a budget. You need to make an appointment. Once you arrive, you must be ready to be examined by an expert, and to have your assumptions challenged. You need to have clear opinions about what you're hearing and experiencing, and to give Russell the feedback he needs to figure out what to do next. You don't have to like or agree with everything he says‚ÄìI didn't‚Äìand when that happened, I told him about it as clearly as I could.

If you are willing to play by these rules, you'll get access to a selection of the very best pianos in the SF bay area, as well as the thoughts and opinions of a person who has decades of experience evaluating pianos and matching them up with the people who are looking for one.

It worked for me, and now I'm the owner of a wonderful piano.

Good luck.</text>< gmapID>

<Gmap_id>0x80857ed1f2457f9f:0xf600dbf352af3223< /Gmap_id><response>None< /response><date>1396059179630</date><review>I went in R. Kassman pianos a few days ago and had a very positive experience. I made an appointment with Russell via email, and then when I showed up, he was cordial and asked me to summarize what I was basically looking for, which I did. He then took me to about 4 or 5 pianos that were in my budget range and asked me play the same thing on all of them, which was a good idea, so I could really tell what was different about each piano. He commented on each of the pianos, explaining why they sounded the way they did. Clearly he's very knowledgeable and passionate about the pianos he carries. I think the best way to describe it is that it was a bit of an "experience", which was pleasant- he was kind of like a tour guide, showing me around the various pianos that he carries. For me, this was the kind of piano shopping experience I hoped to have. He also didn't come across as a high pressure salesperson either.

I believe Russell treats his pianos as one might think of fine wines. He also mentioned to me that he hand-selects many of the pianos he carries, rather than calling the manufacturer and simply saying "Send me another model xyz." So he has a personal connection to them. I think you will have a positive shopping experience if you keep these things in mind:

1) Ask first before playing a particular piano. He keeps the lids closed when they're not being played to keep them in great shape.

2) It's probably better to make an appointment first, rather than just showing up, so that he has the the proper time to show you around while in his shop, and you get his undivided attention.

3) Have some idea of what it is you're looking for & your budget range, but also keep an open mind, trust your ears, & be open to a little piano "education" while you're there. Expect your experience to be different from most of your piano-buying shopping trips.

4) It would also be a good idea to research some of the makes that Russell carries, as many of them are high-end boutique European brands that are top-notch, but may be unfamiliar to the average buyer, such Estonia, Sauter, Steingraeber & Sohne, & Grotrian. If you're a Yamaha lover, this might not be the right place for you.

One more point: I think a good analogy might be that many Americans go and visit France, then come back saying "The French are so rude!" but that's because they expect every French person to speak English to them & they haven't bothered making an effort to do some homework & learn a few key French phrases before making the trip.

Hope that helps.< /review></record>

<time>1396753037137<//time>< Review>
I have gone shopping to R. Kassman twice now, looking for a piano for my daughter. Both times I had set up an appointment, and both times Russell spent a huge amount of time with my daughter, taking her from piano to piano, letting her play, asking what she liked and did not like about each piano, and explaining what is unique about the various pianos ...  The whole journey was peppered with knowledgable and informative comments from an expert. You can tell that Russell is honing in on the likes and dislikes, and trying to guide you towards pianos that match your tonal preferences. My recommendation: if you are shopping for a piano in the area, do pay them a visit. Go there with some time in hand. The Russell tour is a fun and learning experience.

Compared to the other dealerships that I have visited, they carry a wide assortment of pianos, both budget-friendly pianos and high-end European pianos like Steingraeber, Estonia, Sauter, Grotrian etc that are not easily found in the same store, if at all. My experience so far -- there is no substitute for a side by side comparison of pianos to get a sense what you really like. Going to a store like this helps making an educated decision about what you really like.

Russell's tour is perhaps a bit unorthodox. The other stores I had visited typically asked me what I wanted to try. At Kassman, it is more an exploration of the what various brands have to offer in your budget range, and figuring out what suits your style and tastes. If you are willing to explore and figure out what you like, Kassman is the place to go to.

As another poster noted, this store is probably not the right one if you want to just want to go from piano to piano on your own, and just try them out without having to talk to anyone. This is definitely not the Target / Walmart shopping experience. Personally I do not think we could have gotten as much out of the process if we were left on our own -- but I understand that different people have different preferences. Russell carries high-end expensive pianos, and he keeps them is top notch shape. So I understand if he is protective about them, and prefers the shopping experience to be guided tour. However I should not be speaking for Russell.

One further note: Post-sales service has also been outstanding. There were some initial issues that surfaced over the first year or so, which is apparently not uncommon for new pianos. Although I had been warned that such minor issues could come up, it was a bit unnerving when these problems surfaced. Russell took care of these issues, and made me feel comfortable that I had chosen the right dealer to get the piano from.< /Review>

< review>
My partner and I (I am a professional musician) were welcomed warmly by Mr. Kassman, and we briefly explained what we wanted (I wished to replace my current piano, whose tone I had never liked after many attempts at voicing and other modifications). He then took us through a thorough exploration of piano timbre as exemplified by his exceptional stock of instruments.

We spent over an hour playing at least 9 or 10 instruments until we found a magnificent piano that matched our tonal desires and other needs (responsiveness, size, etc.) Mr. Kassman then offered a significant discount from the list price (which was quite unusual for the brand of instrument we purchased, I learned from my research.) We went home and after several hours of contemplation, contacted him with our decision. He stayed open after his posted hours for our return visit to finalize the purchase.

The remainder of our dealings continued to show Mr. Kassman as a generous, professional, and canny businessman. He wrote a very complete and useful appraisal of my old piano. The moving company he uses provided the most careful and complete piano-moving experience I have ever witnessed (and I've seen MANY!) - they spent a half-hour just polishing the instrument (with the included cleaning kit) after placing it in my studio!

I was also pleasantly surprised that the de-humidifier I had briefly mentioned I wanted had been installed and included in the purchase at no charge. And the technician who provided the initial free tuning and voicing spent over two hours at my home, carefully addressing everything I had noted in my first weeks of playing. I also received a follow up call from Mr. Kassman, who wanted to be sure I was satisfied with my purchase.

In response to some reviews on Yelp: I do believe it is important to research piano-buying in advance of such a major purchase. Purchasing from Kassman Pianos is analogous to a purchase from Tiffany or Saks, not to one from Target or Walmart. There is nothing wrong with the latter stores, but an informed consumer will understand the quality of product and service s/he can expect at Kassman Piano. A high-end jeweler will only allow a few items of value to be perused by a customer at any one time, and other customers are asked to wait or return when they can be helped completely. Such is the expectation one should have when purchasing the highest quality instruments made, which are what Mr. Kassman sells.

In sum, I have been exceptionally pleased with every aspect of my experience with Kassman Pianos, and would not hesitate to recommend Russell and his establishment to any serious buyer of a high quality instrument.</review>

< Text>
This one of my favorite thrift shops in the Bay Area! March 24, 2021, yesterday, they were open from 10-1. They had someone at the door checking people in. Only 20 in at one time. It is located in Los Gatos‚Äîa high end place.

The thrift store is not very large, but it is filled with lots of amazing treasures. This ia one of the two thrift shops in town. What do you think women in town do with their designer clothes when they are tired of them?

There are shoes and hand bags locked in glass cases And nice ladies will open them for you so you can have closer look. If you are on a close budget‚Äîthey have blouses for $4. Up high on the wall there are designer jackets that don't look worn. There is a rack of Vintage Clothing, and one of Maternity clothing. There is clothing for children and men, but it seems to me that it is mostly women that will score there. Today, they had a display of dolls that were marked 1/2 off. Need glasses or dishes? They have them. They also have knick knacks and jewelery. If you like reading books‚Äîthey have a lot, but I didn't have time to check them out.

Last but not least, they have dragons!!! I think you might find one that would make a child happy or the child within jolly! A great place to shop for yourself or someone special. I am sorry that I didn't have more time to shop there. Oh, well, another day‚Ä¶< /Text>

<Response>None<//Response>< review>
There's nothing like a thrift shop in an affluent town, this is a true spot for treasure hunting, get an Armani blazer for $10 or grab some fine china for dirt cheap. They have electronics, shoes, and kids clothes galore. It's very tiny and the staff is 100% volunteer. The majority of them are elderly, so service is not that great, but the finds are. They have two dressing rooms and horrible parking. Hours are limited, and you would be best to bring your own bags. The store is 100% charitable as they fund EMQ childrens counseling services for Santa Clara county.</review>

<Rate>4< /Rate><review>As airport food goes, Urban Crave is pretty good. I wouldn't go out of my way for this if it were outside of an airport I fly out of 3-4 times per month. But, as far as breakfast is concerned, this is a decent spot previously in Terminal 2 of SAN and now in Terminal 1. A Bloody Mary and the "Yuppie Wrap" was my usual Monday 6am meal before they moved to Terminal 1. The Yuppie Wrap is a wrap that contains bacon, eggs, cheese, avocado, and fries.  (Kudos to them for not trying to claim this is a burrito.) I usually hold the fries -- not for taste reasons -- but because it makes the wrap too heavy for my first meal of the work week.

When I've flown out of SAN in non-morning hours (which is rare), I've ordered the chili hot dog, which is humongous and also decent -- better than most pub hot dogs.

Best yet, none of Urban Crave's food has resulted in an unfortunate lavatory visit during any of my long trans-con flights.

My biggest complaint about this place is that it is slightly over-priced, even for airport restaurants. Given the lack of reasonable alternatives, I deal with it.

If you like your Bloody Marys spicy, be sure to tell them that when you order.< /review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNgEZta2VwcHU1eVaX9LWwZjuU93pPhPHh2Zmq3=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMiDs9Q41fdtz_JACMuRSp2-xvlVH3Df5ry9qrf=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPK8p7XAw1h2DWIK2SYXkW_it83TwqRyqEBUEcD=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOCe4KD4RhCZ0C4Om_D6B8WwVtwP6VF_ao9P1bj=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMFioW_TfKcHQlMi1KIuWUHCLuGKhPAMs6fkvk1=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPvEb4MEuk5r0YtOJk8YlOsx_wtq0spMlj9KpDK=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOLbsd0EWAg9wWMABIS3kusBqM-VpFUJB5CSndd=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMBh95mVbdhGwQcfUup4bIn2e0x41NvfgEsASOh=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOyGCAR1d-ZfQdsaR13BfDLqsi-Uh4Oce7mPqWO=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics>< resp>

<GmapID>0x80deab161457878f:0xd0f5913466b408bb<//GmapID><rating>1<//rating><text>A greasy airport American grill disguising itself as "Authentic street food".
Only craving you'll have is to be anywhere else.  God knows they're only in business due to lack of any competition.
Atmosphere:  Crowded, as expected for the sole terminal eatery.  No blame here.
Selection:  Despite the name, there's nothing outside of your typical American grill fare.  Such a shame for a city known being a foodie hotspot.  Hardly anything for lighter meals.
Presentation:  Has the brilliant idea to serve everything on the same pie trays, whether it be sides, apps, or entrees.  Points for nostalgia if you've been to prison.
Food:  I had the fried chicken strips and side salad.  Chicken was processed as hell, pretty sure was frozen prepared, and not freshly fried at all.  Fries were soggy.  I'd be happier if I had gotten McDonald's.  Salad was alright.
Service:  Not especially attentive.  Could of used some more waiters for how busy it was.
Price:  'Hurt me' airport prices as expected.
Conclusion- if you really want to eat in T1, bring some takeout through TSA.< /text></record>

<Date>1410404695130< /Date><rate>3</rate>< Review>
Try as I might, I couldn't avoid a hair trim much longer as my hair was soon looking like overgrown weeds. Upon recommendation from a good friend I decided to check out Silver Scissors. The infamous Kathy was booked for the day (even though it was Wednesday) so I decided to go with Ruby. I like the fact that this is a no frills salon and my stylist didn't spend the whole time making small talk. My hair and touch up was $60+ tip. However after coming home I did feel that my haircut was unevenly layered and not blended in as some chunks of hair was hanging more heavily than others, probably since she used a RAZOR to cut my hair! I returned the next week and Ruby fixed it for me, free of charge. However my search continues for a salon to call my own!</Review>

< review>
I actually rarely get my hair cut because I like growing my hair long. If necessary, I usually ask my mom to trim my hair for me or I do it myself. The only times I have ever been to a professional hair cutting studio was when I was in Taiwan. But this summer, my long hair was bother me a lot. My friend recommended this place to me, and I quickly made an appointment. I specifically requested Kathy to cut my hair, (and she is really busy!) so I had to wait a few days before I could be squeezed in. (I was actually wanting Veronica Miller to cut my hair, but when I gave her a call, she was incredibly rude and demeaning. Thankfully Kathy was super sweet!)

Silver Scissors is in the same lot as Chuck E. Cheese's. There's plenty of parking, so if you do come during busy hours, you should be able to secure a spot. Even though I had scheduled an appointment, I had to wait about 20 minutes before Kathy was finished with the client before me. When I walked in, I actually had no clue as to who Kathy was, so I pretty much sat there until somebody called me over. There was a good amount of people waiting in the waiting area - maybe about 5 to 6, but there were about 4-5 stylists cutting hair, so wait doesn't get too long.

I was a bit nervous, seeing as how it had been a long time since getting my hair cut, but everybody was super chill and accommodating. After getting my hair washed , I told Kathy how many inches I wanted to cut off and gave her some clue as to how I wanted my hair to be cut - I honestly didn't know myself. She did a really good job though, and wiped away all of my nerves. I asked for a layered haircut that would be able to frame my face. It seemed like she cut away a lot of hair, but I was really happy with the end result. And then she blew dried my hair for a long time, adding finishing touches, before somebody else took over with the blow drying. At the end, she came back and added some special hair lotion. I was pretty darn happy!

A hair wash, cut and blow dry styled hair came out to be $18 I believe. I think that's a great price! Will definitely be back to get my hair cut with Kathy!< /review>
